        
        ---
        
        # **14. Rental Logic**
        
        ✔ Supported
        
        ✔ Owners of rental properties can upload surveys
        
        ✔ Home-Hunters browsing rental listings can buy surveys
        
        ✔ Admin flow identical
        
        Surveys are **universally supported** for buyers and owners, independent of sale or rent.
        
        ---
        
    - **🧩 WF-A7 — Support Inbox (Admin + Support Staff)**
        
        > Central place where **all user questions & issues**
        > 
        
        ---
        
        ## **1. Designer Checklist**
        
        - Use **Dashfolio+** main layout with:
            - Left column: **ticket list**
            - Right column: **conversation + user context**
        - Keep layout **3-part on desktop**:
            1. Filters/top summary row
            2. Ticket list
            3. Conversation + meta sidebar
        - Mobile: stack to ticket list → tap → conversation.
        - Use pill-style filters: All · Open · Pending · Closed · Urgent.
        - Use subtle colour coding:
            - Status chips (Open, Pending, Closed)
            - Priority chips (Low, Normal, Urgent)
        - Keep icons minimal: envelope (email), WhatsApp, info, warning.
        
        ---
        
        ## **2. Developer Checklist**
        
        - Build endpoints:
            - GET /admin/support/tickets
            - GET /admin/support/tickets/{ticketID}
            - POST /admin/support/tickets/{ticketID}/reply
            - POST /admin/support/tickets/{ticketID}/update (status, priority, assignment)
        - Ticket sources:
            - Contact form
            - “Support” footer link
            - Owner & Home-Hunter “Need help?” buttons
            - System alerts (auto-created, Phase 2)
        - Each ticket must be linkable to:
            - ownerID OR hunterID (if known)
            - listing / propertyID (if relevant)
            - integration error (optional)
        - Log all admin/staff actions for audit.
        
        ---
        
        ## **3. Admin Journey (Short Summary)**
        
        Admin/support arrives here when:
        
        - They click **Support Inbox** in the Admin sidebar (A7).
        - They click “Open in Support” from:
            - A2 Owner Detail
            - A3 Home-Hunter Detail
            - A1 Dashboard alert
            - A4 Integrations error that needs manual reply
        
        From here they **read, reply, reassign, and close tickets**.
        
        ---
        
        ## **4. User Journey (Where This Page Sits)**
        
        ```
        A1 Dashboard
           ↓ Alerts (Support / Errors)
        A7 Support Inbox
           ↓
        Ticket → Reply → Close / Escalate → Logged
        ```
        
        ---
        
        ## **5. Purpose**
        
        Give you and any support staff **one unified place** to:
        
        - See who needs help (owners & home-hunters)
        - Prioritise issues
        - Reply quickly
        - Assign tickets to specific team members
        - See context (who they are, what they’re doing)
        - Avoid losing conversations inside scattered emails/WhatsApp threads
        
        ---
        
        ## **6. What This Page Should Solve**
        
        - “What’s on fire right now?” (Urgent)
        - “Which tickets are waiting on us?”
        - “Which users are stuck in important flows? (listing, booking, offers)”
        - “Can support see enough context to answer in 1 message?”
        - “Can we track response time & quality later?”
        
        ---
        
        ## **7. What the Designer Should Build in Framer**
        
        ### **7.1 Top Bar — Support KPIs (small cards)**
        
        - Open tickets (count)
        - Urgent tickets (count)
        - Avg first response time (MVP: simple number)
        - Tickets today
        
        Each is a small card at the top.
        
        ---
        
        ### **7.2 Left Column — Ticket List**
        
        A scrollable list with filters above.
        
        **Filters:**
        
        - Status: All / Open / Pending / Closed
        - Priority: All / Normal / Urgent
        - Source: Form / WhatsApp / Email / System
        - Role: Owner / Home-Hunter / Unknown
        
        **Ticket Row Layout:**
        
        - Status chip (Open / Pending / Closed)
        - Priority chip (Normal / Urgent)
        - Short subject line
        - Who: Name (Owner / Home-Hunter) + role tag
        - Time since last update
        
        Example row:
        
        > [Open] [Urgent]
        > 
        
        > “Calendar link not working for my viewing”
        > 
        
        > Alex Johnson · Owner · 2h ago
        > 
        
        ---
        
        ### **7.3 Right Column — Conversation + Context**
        
        ### **A) Conversation Panel**
        
        - Ticket subject at top
        - Source (Email / WhatsApp / Web Form)
        - Message thread (chat-style bubbles):
            - User messages
            - Admin replies
        
        Controls at bottom:
        
        - Reply box
        - Quick reply templates (Phase 2)
        - Attach file (optional later)
        - Change status (Open → Pending → Closed)
        - Set priority
        - Assign to staff member
        
        ### **B) Context Sidebar (Right side, narrow)**
        
        - User type: Owner / Home-Hunter / Unknown
        - Link to:
            - “View Owner Profile (A2)” OR
            - “View Home-Hunter Profile (A3)”
        - Related context:
            - Linked property (if in inquiry)
            - Linked viewing/offer (if exists)
        - Last actions:
            - Last login
            - Last viewing booked
            - Last listing change
        
        ---
        
        ## **8. Developer Requirements**
        
        ### **MVP**
        
        - Tickets stored in support_tickets table:
            - id, userID (nullable), role, subject, status, priority, source, createdAt, updatedAt
        - Messages in support_messages:
            - ticketID, sender (user/admin), text, createdAt
        - Link to related entities via:
            - ownerID
            - hunterID
            - propertyID
            - integrationID (optional)
        - Basic notification:
            - Email or WhatsApp to user when replied
        - Status transitions:
            - Open → Pending → Closed
        
        ### **Phase 2**
        
        - SLA timers (breached/ok)
        - AI-suggested replies
        - Auto-tagging topics
        - Triggerable macros (e.g. “send instructions for uploading EPC”)
        - Internal-only notes per ticket
        
        ---
        
        ## **9. KPI Definitions (Support)**
        
        On this page or in A1/A9 later:
        
        - Open Tickets
        - Urgent Tickets
        - First Response Time
        - Resolution Time
        - Tickets per Owner / Hunter
        - Topic distribution (Phase 2)
        
        ---
        
        ## **10. Conversion Funnel (Support Impact, Phase 2)**
        
        Not shown as a visual yet, but conceptually:
        
        > Blocked User → Ticket Created → Support Reply → Issue Resolved → User completes flow (listing, booking, offer)
        > 
        
        Helps you see how support improves conversion.
        
        ---
        
        ## **11. Permission Logic**
        
        | **Action** | **Admin** | **Support Staff** | **Founder** | **Dev-only** |
        | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
        | View all tickets | ✔ | ✔ | ✔ | ✔ |
        | Reply to tickets | ✔ | ✔ | ✔ | ✖ |
        | Change status / priority | ✔ | ✔ | ✔ | ✖ |
        | Assign to team member | ✔ | ✔ | ✔ | ✖ |
        | Delete ticket | ✔ | ✖ | ✔ | ✖ |
        | View linked user profiles | ✔ | ✔ | ✔ | ✔ |
        
        ---
        
        ## **12. Developer Tooling Overview**
        
        - Tables:
            - support_tickets
            - support_messages
            - users (owners + hunters)
            - properties
            - system_events (for auto-generated tickets in Phase 2)
        - Join points:
            - Many tickets ↔ 1 user
            - 1 ticket ↔ 1 property (optional)
        - Ensure logging of:
            - who replied
            - when
            - old status → new status
        
        ---
        
        ## **13. Dummy Content (for designers)**
        
        **Ticket list examples:**
        
        - [Open] [Urgent] “Viewing link not working” — Owner — 2h ago
        - [Pending] [Normal] “Can’t upload EPC document” — Owner — 5h ago
        - [Closed] [Normal] “How do I change my price?” — Home-Hunter — 1d ago
        
        **Conversation preview:**
        
        > User:
        > 
        
        > “Hi, I tried to book a viewing for 12 King Street but the calendar shows an error.”
        > 
        
        > 
        > 
        
        > Support (Yalla):
        > 
        
        > “Thanks for flagging this. We’ve refreshed the connection now. Could you please try again? If it still doesn’t work, we can book it manually for you.”
        > 
        
        ---
        
        ## **14. Rental Logic (Integrated)**
        
        Support Inbox doesn’t care if the context is sale or rent.
        
        The linked entities (property/offer/application) will carry that info.
        
        ---
        
    - **🧩 WF-A8 — Billing & Revenue (Admin)**
        
        *(All money in, all money out, all subscriptions, all payouts — ONE PLACE.)*
        
        ---
        
        # **1. Designer Checklist**
        
        - Use Dashfolio+ card + table layout
        - Page layout sections:
            1. Top KPI row
            2. Income tables
            3. Outgoing costs
            4. Subscriptions overview
            5. Manual adjustment panel (Phase 2)
        - Use Yalla Yellow ONLY for:
            - CTA buttons
            - Highlights (e.g., “Overdue”)
        - Use icons: £, subscription, warning, calendar, checkmark.
        - Include filters: Date range, Product, Country.
        - Keep charts minimal (bar chart + pie chart).
        
        ---
        
        # **2. Developer Checklist (MVP)**
        
        ### **Back-end / Data**
        
        - Create tables:
            - billing_transactions (all charges & payouts)
            - subscriptions (owner plans)
            - services_orders (signs, photography, EPC, etc.)
            - external_costs (Rightmove, WhatsApp, Twilio, hosting)
            - payouts (survey marketplace payouts)
        - Pull from Stripe:
            - Customer name
            - Product
            - Amount
            - Status (paid / unpaid / refunded)
            - Invoice URL
        - Link every billable event to:
            - ownerID
            - hunterID (if survey purchase)
            - propertyID
            - serviceID
            - surveyID
        
        ### **Front-end**
        
        - Filters + pagination
        - Charts (use a simple open-source library or Framer embed)
        - CSV export for accounting
        
        ### **Automations**
        
        - Monthly “Billing Digest” email to founder
        - Stripe webhook integration:
            - Renewals
            - Failed payments
            - Refunds
        
        ---
        
        # **3. Admin Journey (Short Summary)**
        
        Admin comes here to:
        
        - See **total revenue**, **subscription income**, **survey marketplace income**
        - See **service orders** (e.g. EPC, sign boards)
        - Track **external outgoing costs** (Rightmove, Twilio, S3 storage)
        - See **profit margin per owner**
        - Run accounting export (monthly)
        
        This page becomes the **financial command center**.
        
        ---
        
        # **4. User Journey (Where This Page Sits)**
        
        ```
        A1 Admin Dashboard
           ↓
        A8 Billing & Revenue
           ↓
        (Income → Subscriptions → Service Orders → Costs → Profit)
        ```
        
        ---
        
        # **5. Purpose**
        
        - Make revenue transparent and easy to manage
        - Track subscriptions & service usage
        - Track expenses
        - Help founders understand **profit**, **burn**, and **runway**
        - Prepare clean accounting exports for HMRC/bookkeeper
        - Watch financial health as Yalla grows
        
        ---
        
        # **6. What This Page Should Solve**
        
        - “How much did we earn this month?”
        - “Which owners bring in the most revenue?”
        - “How much do we spend on integrations?”
        - “What’s the profit margin?”
        - “Which subscriptions failed to renew?”
        - “Are we losing money on Rightmove packages?”
        - “How did survey marketplace perform?”
        - “What was purchased today?”
        
        ---
        
        # **7. What the Designer Should Build in Framer**
        
        ### **7.1 Top KPI Row (Cards)**
        
        Cards:
        
        - **Total Revenue (This Month)**
        - **Subscriptions Revenue**
        - **Service Orders Revenue**
        - **Survey Marketplace Revenue**
        - **Outgoing Costs**
        - **Net Profit**
        
        Secondary metric:
        
        - Monthly Growth % (small tag)
        
        ---
        
        ### **7.2 Section A — Incoming Revenue (Table)**
        
        Columns:
        
        | **Date** | **Customer** | **Product** | **Amount** | **Country** | **Status** | **Invoice** |
        | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
        
        Products:
        
        - Subscription
        - Add-on service (Photography, EPC, Sign Board, etc.)
        - Survey purchase
        - Offer Boost (Phase 2)
        
        UX:
        
        - Click row → open invoice modal
        - Invoice modal shows:
            - Billing name
            - Itemized list
            - Stripe link
        
        ---
        
        ### **7.3 Section B — Subscriptions Overview**
        
        A separate table:
        
        | Owner | Plan | Renew Date | Payment Status | Next Invoice | Notes |
        
        Green = active
        
        Yellow = retrying
        
        Red = unpaid
        
        ---
        
        ### **7.4 Section C — Outgoing Costs (Integrations)**
        
        Table:
        
        | **Date** | **Vendor** | **Category** | **Amount** | **Billing Cycle** | **Notes** |
        | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
        
        Vendors:
        
        - Rightmove
        - OnTheMarket
        - Twilio
        - WhatsApp Business
        - S3 Storage
        - Cloud hosting
        - Accounting software
        - Design subscriptions (if any)
        
        ---
        
        ### **7.5 Section D — Profit & Cost Chart**
        
        - Simple bar chart:
            - Revenue vs Expenses (monthly)
        - Pie chart:
            - Expense breakdown by vendor
        
        ---
        
        ### **7.6 Section E — Export Tools**
        
        Buttons:
        
        - **Export CSV (Monthly)**
        - **Export CSV (All time)**
        - **Send to Accountant** (mailto with attached CSV)
        
        ---
        
        # **8. Developer Requirements**
        
        ### **Reporting Logic**
        
        - “This Month” = first day of current month → today
        - Group revenue by:
            - Subscription
            - Services
            - Marketplace (surveys)
        - Group expenses by:
            - Vendor
            - Category
        
        ### **IDs**
        
        - transactionID
        - subscriptionID
        - serviceID
        - payoutID
        
        ### **Join**
        
        - transaction ↔ owner
        - transaction ↔ property
        - transaction ↔ survey
        - transaction ↔ service order
        
        ### **Error Handling**
        
        - Flag if Stripe webhook fails
        - Show “Retry Payment” button for failed invoices
        
        ---
        
        # **9. KPI Definitions**
        
        - **MRR**: Monthly Recurring Revenue
        - **ARPU**: Average Revenue Per Owner
        - **Gross Margin**: Revenue – direct listing costs
        - **CAC** (Phase 2): Customer acquisition cost
        - **Expense run-rate**: Total monthly expenses
        - **Survey revenue share**: Yalla % vs uploader %
        
        ---
        
        # **10. Funnel Overview (Billing)**
        
        ```
        Owner signs up → Buys subscription → Lists place → Orders services
                                             ↓
                                  Survey sales generate passive revenue
                                             ↓
                              Subscriptions renew + additional revenue
                                             ↓
                                      Admin sees full overview (A8)
        ```
        
        ---
        
        # **11. ID Logic**
        
        Everything gets IDs:
        
        - billingTransactionID
        - subscriptionID
        - listingServiceOrderID
        - surveyPurchaseID
        - payoutID
        
        ---
        
        # **12. Developer Tooling**
        
        - Stripe dashboard
        - Stripe webhooks
        - Database tables (billing, costs, subscriptions)
        - accountant@… email integration
        - CSV export builder
        
        ---
        
        # **13. Dummy Content (for designers)**
        
        ```
        Total Revenue (This Month): £4,280
        Subscriptions: £1,920
        Service Orders: £1,560
        Survey Marketplace: £800
        Outgoing Costs: £620
        Net Profit: £3,660
        ```
        
        **Example revenue row:**
        
        ```
        12 Mar 2025 | Alice K. | Subscription (Pro Seller) | £12 | UK | Paid | View Invoice
        ```
        
        **Outgoing cost:**
        
        ```
        03 Mar 2025 | Rightmove | Listings Feed | £299 | Monthly | Auto-paid
        ```
        
        ---
        
        # **14. Rental Logic**
        
        Same as WF-O flows — rental owners also have:
        
        - subscriptions
        - service orders
        - expenses allocated to their listings
        
        Survey marketplace excluded.
        
        ---
        
    - **🧩 WF-A9 — Analytics & Performance Dashboard (Admin)**
        
        *(Bird’s-eye view of everything: conversion, revenue, marketplace, listings, funnels.)*
        
        # **1. Designer Checklist**
        
        - Use Dashfolio+ layout
        - Top “selector bar” for time period:
            
            **7d · 30d · 90d · YTD · Custom**
            
        - Use two layers of visualisation:
            1. **Global KPIs** (cards)
            2. **Graphs** (line, bar, funnel, pie)
        - Tables underneath graphs for detail:
            - Top-performing listings
            - Lowest-performing listings
            - Survey marketplace stats
            - Owner churn
            - User behaviour
        - Use Yalla Yellow to highlight positive momentum.
        - Use red only for negative KPIs (drop-offs, errors).
        - Must be mobile-friendly (stack cards).
        
        ---
        
        # **2. Developer Checklist**
        
        ### **Data Sources Needed:**
        
        - Page views + source referral data
        - Inquiries → viewings → offers → applications
        - Subscription renewals and cancellations
        - Survey marketplace upload → approval → purchase data
        - Error logs (A4) — rate per week
        - Support tickets (A7) — response times
        
        ### **MVP Requirements:**
        
        - Daily aggregated metrics table
        - Basic chart API
        - Funnel generation logic
        - Referral tracking
        - Geo tracking (optional)
        
        ### **Phase 2:**
        
        - Predictive analytics
        - User scoring
        - Revenue forecasting
        - AI anomaly detection
        
        ---
        
        # **3. Admin Journey (Short Summary)**
        
        Admin arrives here to:
        
        - Understand **conversion health**
        - Measure **funnel leaks** (views → inquiries → viewings → offers)
        - Track **survey marketplace performance**
        - See **subscription trends**
        - Understand **owner behaviour**
        - Discover **top-performing listings**
        - Compare **rent vs sale trends**
        
        This is the “command center” for decision-making.
        
        ---
        
        # **4. User Journey (Where this page sits)**
        
        ```
        A1 Dashboard
           ↓
        A9 Admin Analytics
           ↓
        Filters → KPIs → Charts → Insights → Actions
        ```
        
        ---
        
        # **5. Purpose**
        
        Provide full visibility into:
        
        - Business health
        - Growth momentum
        - Conversion funnels
        - Revenue consistency
        - Survey marketplace usage
        - User behaviour
        - Operational bottlenecks
        
        This is how you decide:
        
        - Where to improve
        - How to scale
        - What to automate
        - When to hire
        - What features to prioritise next
        
        ---
        
        # **6. What This Page Should Solve**
        
        - Which listings perform best?
        - Where do leads come from?
        - What sources drive the most offers?
        - How many viewings convert to offers?
        - Are there weak spots in the owner journey?
        - Are subscription renewals declining?
        - Are users stuck in onboarding?
        - Which services drive the most revenue?
        - What’s the return rate of surveys?
        - Are there systemic errors (calendar, WhatsApp, feeds)?
        
        ---
        
        # **7. What the Designer Should Build in Framer**
        
        ## **7.1 Top KPI Bar (cards)**
        
        - Total Listings (Live)
        - Total Inquiries (period)
        - Total Viewings Booked
        - Total Offers Sent
        - Conversion Rate (views → offers)
        - Avg Time to Offer
        - Survey Marketplace Revenue
        - Subscription Renewal Rate
        - Support SLA % (responses < 24h)
        - Integration Health Score
        
        Each card shows % change vs previous period.
        
        ---
        
        ## **7.2 Conversion Funnel (core visual)**
        
        ```
        Views
           ↓ (CTR)
        Inquiries
           ↓ (Booking Rate)
        Viewings
           ↓ (Offer Rate)
        Offers
           ↓ (Acceptance Rate)
        Sales / Lets Completed
        ```
        
        For Rent:
        
        - “Applications” instead of “Offers”.
        
        Graph: A stepped funnel with numbers + percentages.
        
        ---
        
        ## **7.3 Lead Sources — Pie Chart**
        
        Segments:
        
        - Yalla.House (organic)
        - Rightmove
        - OnTheMarket
        - Zoopla
        - WhatsApp
        - Sign Board (QR scans)
        - Direct (URL typed)
        - Shared links
        
        Click each → table appears:
        
        | Source | Views | Inquiries | Bookings | Offers | Conversion % |
        
        ---
        
        ## **7.4 Marketplace Analytics**
        
        Show:
        
        - Surveys uploaded
        - Surveys approved
        - Survey sales
        - Marketplace revenue
        - Uploader payout totals
        - Avg sale price
        - Survey reuse rate per property
        
        Graph:
        
        - Line graph: uploads vs sales over time
        
        ---
        
        ## **7.5 Listing Performance Table**
        
        | Place | Views | Inquiries | Viewings | Offers | Conversion % | Avg Response Time |
        
        Sort by:
        
        - Best performing
        - Worst performing
        - Needs attention
        
        ---
        
        ## **7.6 Owner Behaviour Metrics**
        
        Show:
        
        - Active owners this week
        - Owners who haven’t logged in for 7+ days
        - Listings stuck in “Draft”
        - Listings missing photos
        - Listings without calendar availability
        
        ---
        
        ## **7.7 Support Metrics (from A7)**
        
        - Open tickets
        - Average first response time
        - SLA compliance
        - Top topic categories
        
        ---
        
        ## **7.8 Integrations Health (from A4)**
        
        Small table:
        
        | **Integration** | **Status** | **Failures 24h** | **Last Success** | **Tendencies** |
        | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
        
        ---
        
        # **8. Developer Requirements**
        
        ### **Data aggregation:**
        
        - Create daily_stats table:
            - date
            - views
            - inquiries
            - viewings
            - offers
            - completions
            - revenue numbers
            - survey metrics
        - API routes for charts:
            - /analytics/traffic
            - /analytics/funnels
            - /analytics/referrals
            - /analytics/marketplace
            - /analytics/errors
        - Must support date-range queries
        - Must support grouping by:
            - day
            - week
            - month
        
        ### **Tracking Requirements:**
        
        - Referral tracking
        - UTM parameters
        - QR code tracking
        - Source on all inquiries
        
        ### **Performance:**
        
        - Cache analytics to avoid heavy DB calls
        - Update nightly via cron job
        
        ---
        
        # **9. KPI Definitions**
        
        - **CTR (Click-through Rate):** Inquiries / Views
        - **Booking rate:** Viewings / Inquiries
        - **Offer rate:** Offers / Viewings
        - **Completion rate:** Sales / Offers
        - **MRR:** Monthly recurring revenue
        - **LTV:** Lifetime value of an owner
        - **Churn rate:** Owners cancelling subscription
        - **CAC:** Customer acquisition cost (Phase 2)
        - **Survey Marketplace Margin:** revenue – payouts
        
        ---
        
        # **10. Conversion Funnel (with numbers + %) example**
        
        ```
        Views: 12,400
        ↓ (12.3%)
        Inquiries: 1,460
        ↓ (42%)
        Viewings: 613
        ↓ (18%)
        Offers: 110
        ↓ (32%)
        Sales Completed: 35
        ```
        
        ---
        
        # **11. ID Logic**
        
        Every event logged as:
        
        - eventID
        - userID
        - placeID
        - sessionID
        - referralSourceID
        
        Enables full funnel tracing.
        
        ---
        
        # **12. Developer Tooling Overview**
        
        - Cron jobs for nightly aggregation
        - Logs stored in:
            - events
            - daily_stats
            - funnels
            - referrals
        - Graphs generated client-side
        - SQL optimized for aggregation
        
        ---
        
        # **13. Dummy Content**
        
        **Top KPIs:**
        
        ```
        Total Listings: 42 (↑ 8%)
        Total Inquiries: 1,460 (↑ 12%)
        Total Viewings: 613 (↑ 5%)
        Total Offers: 110 (↑ 7%)
        Survey Marketplace Revenue: £740 (↑ 33%)
        Subscription Renewal Rate: 96%
        ```
        
        ---
        
        # **14. Rental Logic**
        
        Rental funnel variant:
        
        ```
        Views → Inquiries → Viewings → Applications → Tenancy Secured
        ```
        
        Same UX, different wording.
        
        ---

        Generate report (disabled)
        
        ---
        
        ### **Compliance & Audit Report**
        
        **Description:**
        
        Exportable records for internal review and compliance checks.
        
        **Action:**
        
        Generate report (disabled)

        | Flagged Issues | — |
        
        **Export options:**
        
        PDF · CSV (disabled)

- **📌 PARKED TOPIC — Agent Discovery & HH Multi-Agent Requests**
    
    ### 
    
    **Status:** Paused, agreed direction
    
    **Key decisions so far:**
    
    - Agent labels:
        - “Available via NoAgent”
        - “Not available via NoAgent (yet)”
    - Hybrid model:
        - Discovered agents (read-only)
        - Soft-partnered agents (contactable)
    - HH submits **one structured request**
    - NoAgent distributes to 10–20 agents
    - Agents must accept to unlock contact
    - HH controls filters & privacy
    - Goal: convert agents via inbound demand, not cold sales
    
    **Next time we need to:**
    
    - Finalise HH request UI copy
    - Finalise agent invite email
    - Lock WF-H1 / WF-H5 updates
    - Decide Phase-2 agent dashboard scope
    
    Then later, your prompt is simply:
    
    > “Continue from the PARKED TOPIC: Agent Discovery & HH Multi-Agent Requests.”
    > 
    
    This is very clean and very “founder-grade”.
    
- Owner HH - Agent Search
    
    x
    
    - **“Agent not partnered with NoAgent” is unclear, defensive, and makes users ask the wrong questions**.
        
        The label should:
        
        - make sense instantly
        - describe **capability**, not relationship
        - avoid sounding commercial or political
        - work for **Owners and Home-Hunters**
        - scale to services + agents later
        
        Below is a **clean, product-native labeling system** that solves this properly.
        
        ---
        
        ## **1️⃣ First: what does “partnered” actually mean in the product?**
        
        Let’s be precise, because the label must reflect this.
        
        ### **In NoAgent terms, “partnered” really means:**
        
        > This agent can receive and respond to requests through NoAgent.
        > 
        
        That’s it.
        
        Not:
        
        - endorsement
        - exclusivity
        - commission
        - special deal
        
        Just **capability + consent**.
        
        So the label should describe **how interaction works**, not the business relationship.
        
        ---
        
        ## **2️⃣ Recommended labels (clear, neutral, user-centric)**
        
        ### **🟢 For agents you CAN interact with through NoAgent**
        
        **Primary label (recommended):**
        
        > Available via NoAgent
        > 
        
        Why this works:
        
        - Describes *what the user can do*
        - Neutral
        - Positive
        - No explanation needed
        
        Alternatives (also good, but slightly weaker):
        
        - “Contactable via NoAgent”
        - “Reachable through NoAgent”
        
        ---
        
        ### **🟡 For agents you CANNOT message through NoAgent (discovered only)**
        
        **Primary label (recommended):**
        
        > Public listing (external)
        > 
        
        or
        
        > Public agent (external)
        > 
        
        Why this works:
        
        - Honest
        - Non-judgmental
        - Clearly explains limitation
        - Familiar language (users know “external links”)
        
        Good alternatives:
        
        - “Listed publicly”
        - “External agent”
        
        ❌ Avoid:
        
        - “Not partnered”
        - “Unavailable”
        - “Inactive”
        - “Unverified”
        
        Those imply blame or quality issues.
        
        ---
        
        ## **3️⃣ How this reads to users (very important)**
        
        ### **Owner perspective**
        
        - *“Ah, these agents I can contact directly here. These others exist, but I’d need to reach out myself or invite them.”*
        - No fear
        - No confusion
        - No pressure
        
        ### **Home-Hunter perspective**
        
        You’re right here: **they mostly don’t care** — as long as:
        
        - messages are in one inbox
        - spam is controlled
        
        So for HHs:
        
        - the label is informational only
        - the primary CTA is always clear
        
        ---
        
        ## **4️⃣ What happens when users click a “Public agent (external)”?**
        
        Instead of a dead end, do this:
        
        ### **CTA text (small, secondary)**
        
        > Invite this agent to NoAgent
        > 
        
        On click:
        
        - Explain in one sentence:
            
            > “This agent isn’t yet reachable through NoAgent. You can invite them so they can receive your request here.”
            > 
        
        This turns a limitation into:
        
        - empowerment
        - organic growth
        - zero spam
        
        ---
        
        ## **5️⃣ Where these labels appear (wireframe mapping)**
        
        ### **WF-O3 — Find Agents**
        
        Agent cards show:
        
        - Name
        - Area
        - Public rating (optional)
        - **Status badge**:
            - 🟢 Available via NoAgent
            - 🟡 Public agent (external)
        
        CTA:
        
        - If 🟢 → “Contact agent”
        - If 🟡 → “Invite agent”
        
        ---
        
        ### **WF-H1 — Home-Hunter Dashboard**
        
        Same labels, same logic.
        
        ---
        
        ### **WF-P7 — Partners**
        
        Explain in plain language:
        
        > “Some agents are available directly through NoAgent.
        > 
        
        > Others are shown for transparency and can be invited if you want to work with them here.”
        > 
        
        No business jargon.
        
        ---
        
        ### **WF-A2 — Users**
        
        Internal statuses stay technical:
        
        - Discovered
        - Soft-partnered
        - Active
        
        But **never shown to end users**.
        
        ---
        
        ## **6️⃣ Do we need to explain “benefits of being available via NoAgent”?**
        
        Yes — but **not on the card**.
        
        ### **Where benefits belong:**
        
        - WF-P7 (Partners page)
        - Invite email
        - Agent-facing copy
        
        ### **NOT:**
        
        - On the search results
        - On Owner / HH flows
        
        End users just want to know:
        
        > “Can I contact them here or not?”
        > 
        
        ---
        
        ## **7️⃣ Summary — lock this in**
        
        **Replace all “partnered / not partnered” wording with:**
        
        - 🟢 **Available via NoAgent**
        - 🟡 **Public agent (external)**
        
        This:
        
        - avoids confusion
        - avoids defensiveness
        - scales to services
        - feels like a real product, not a startup workaround
        
        If you want, next I can:
        
        - update the **exact agent card microcopy**
        - write the **Invite Agent modal copy**
        - or align this with **service providers** so it’s one unified model
        
        This was a very good catch — fixing this now saves a lot of UX debt later.
        
    - **Hybrid “Discover + Partner” Agents**
        
        Think of agents in **three visible states**, not one.
        
        ---
        
        ## **🟡 Agent States (very important)**
        
        ### **1️⃣**
        
        ### **Discovered agents**
        
        ### **(not partnered yet)**
        
        - Pulled from **public sources** (Google Maps / business listings)
        - Read-only
        - Clearly labelled
        - No direct contact through NoAgent
        
        ### **2️⃣**
        
        ### **Soft-partnered agents**
        
        - Agent acknowledged NoAgent
        - Listed with richer profile
        - Can receive structured introductions
        
        ### **3️⃣**
        
        ### **Fully partnered agents**
        
        ### **(Phase 2)**
        
        - Dashboard access
        - Analytics
        - Optional integrations
        
        This removes the “empty marketplace” problem immediately.
        
        ---
        
        # **1️⃣ How “Discovered agents” works (Phase 1, fast)**
        
        ### **Source**
        
        - Google Places API **(not scraping websites)**
        - Business listing data:
            - name
            - address
            - postcode
            - category (“estate agent”)
            - Google rating (optional, public data)
        
        ⚠️ This is **lookup**, not scraping — much safer.
        
        ---
        
        ### **How they appear in the UI**
        
        Agent card shows:
        
        - Agency name
        - Area
        - Public Google rating (if available)
        - Status badge:
            
            > 🟡 “Not partnered with NoAgent”
            > 
        
        CTA:
        
        > “Invite this agent to NoAgent”
        > 
        
        ---
        
        ### **What users can do**
        
        - Owners / HH can:
            - see agents exist in their area
            - understand the local landscape
        - They **cannot**:
            - message them via NoAgent
            - share their profile yet
        
        This sets expectations correctly.
        
        ---
        
        # **2️⃣ Soft-partnered agents (your current plan, but lighter)**
        
        ### **How they become soft-partnered**
        
        - You invite them
        - OR an Owner / HH invites them
        - OR they accept a generic invite
        
        ### **What changes**
        
        - Badge becomes:
            
            > 🟢 “Available via NoAgent”
            > 
        - Contact modal unlocks
        - Structured intro enabled
        
        Still no dashboard needed.
        
        ---
        
        # **3️⃣ Why this is much better than “manual only”**
        
        ### **✅ Speed**
        
        - City-level coverage instantly
        - No waiting to seed manually
        
        ### **✅ Honesty**
        
        - No fake listings
        - Clear labels
        - No bait-and-switch
        
        ### **✅ Trust**
        
        - Users see reality
        - Agents aren’t misrepresented
        - No legal grey zones
        
        ### **✅ Scalability**
        
        - Countries, not postcodes
        - Manual work only for **conversion**, not discovery
        
        ---
        
        # **4️⃣ How this affects your wireframes (clear + limited)**
        
        ### **🧩 WF-O3 — Find Agents**
        
        - Show two sections:
            - “Agents available via NoAgent”
            - “Other agents in your area”
        
        Greyed cards for discovered agents.
        
        ---
        
        ### **🧩 WF-H1 — Home-Hunter Dashboard**
        
        Same pattern:
        
        - Discover agents
        - Soft-partnered highlighted
        
        ---
        
        ### **🧩 WF-P7 — Partners**
        
        Add explanation:
        
        > “We show public agents in your area for transparency.
        > 
        
        > Only agents partnered with NoAgent can be contacted through the platform.”
        > 
        
        ---
        
        ### **🧩 WF-A2 — Users**
        
        - Agent status field:
            - Discovered
            - Soft-partnered
            - Active
        
        ---
        
        ## **⚠️ What NOT to do**
        
        - ❌ Don’t allow messaging to non-partnered agents
        - ❌ Don’t fake ratings
        - ❌ Don’t auto-email agents without consent
        - ❌ Don’t scrape private data
        
        ---
        
        # **5️⃣ Ratings — how to handle this cleanly**
        
        ### **Phase 1**
        
        - Use **public Google rating only**
        - Label clearly:

            > 
        
        ### **Phase 2**
        
        - Internal NoAgent feedback
        - Optional later public scores
        
        This avoids disputes.

        - Discovered photographers / EPC / surveyors
        - Greyed out
        - Invite CTA
        - Upgrade to partner

    - HH sends to many Agents via NoAgent
        
        Yes — and you’re thinking about this **exactly the right way**.
        
        The trick is to make this feel like **one smart request**, not “messaging 10–20 agents”, and to turn it into a **conversion funnel for NoAgent**, not spam.
        
        Below is a **clean, scalable, HH-friendly system** that works in Phase 1 and becomes very powerful in Phase 2.
        
        ---
        
        # **The right model:**
        
        # **One Request → Many Agents (via NoAgent)**
        
        ## **Core rule (lock this in)**
        
        👉 **Home-Hunters never message agents individually.**
        
        👉 They submit **one structured request**.
        
        👉 NoAgent distributes it **selectively and safely**.
        
        This protects:
        
        - HH from spam
        - Agents from noise
        - You from legal / trust issues
        
        ---
        
        ## **1️⃣ HH flow — what the user actually experiences**
        
        ### **Step 1 — HH creates a “Request for Help”**
        
        This lives in:
        
        - **WF-H1 (Dashboard)** or
        - **WF-H5 (Offers & Applications)**
        
        Button:
        
        > Get help from local agents
        > 
        
        ---
        
        ### **Step 2 — Structured request (not free text)**
        
        The HH fills **one short form**:
        
        **Required**
        
        - Buy or Rent
        - Area(s)
        - Budget range
        - Timeline
        - Verification status (already known)
        
        **Optional**
        
        - Property types
        - Must-haves
        - Notes (max 300 chars)
        
        **Privacy controls (important)**
        
        - ☐ Email only
        - ☐ No calls
        - ☐ Only agents working in my budget
        - ☐ No marketing messages
        
        CTA:
        
        > Send request
        > 
        
        ---
        
        ## **2️⃣ What NoAgent does with this request (smart part)**
        
        ### **Phase 1 distribution logic (simple + safe)**
        
        - Match HH request against:
            - agent coverage area
            - sales / rental focus
            - status = **Available via NoAgent**
        - Select **max 10–20 agents** automatically
        - Send **one structured intro email** per agent
        
        Agents receive:
        
        - anonymised summary
        - clear intent
        - clear filters
        - **Accept / Decline** CTA
        
        No contact details yet.
        
        ---
        
        ## **3️⃣ What agents see (why they engage)**
        
        Subject example:
        
        > New verified buyer request in your area (via NoAgent)
        > 
        
        Email includes:
        
        - Buyer type (cash / mortgage ready / renting)
        - Budget
        - Area
        - Timeline
        - Conditions (email only, etc.)
        
        CTA:
        
        - ✅ Accept request
        - ❌ Decline
        
        This feels:
        
        - qualified
        - respectful
        - low effort
        
        ---
        
        ## **4️⃣ What happens when agents accept**
        
        ### **Phase 1 behaviour**
        
        - Agent accepts → contact unlocked
        - HH notified:
            
            > “3 agents are available to help you”
            > 
        - Communication can move:
            - via NoAgent inbox (later)
            - or email (Phase 1)
        
        HH **never gets flooded**:
        
        - agents cannot message unless accepted
        - HH can close the request anytime
        
        ---
        
        ## **5️⃣ Where this lures agents into NoAgent (key part)**
        
        After an agent accepts, they see:
        
        > “Respond faster and manage requests directly inside NoAgent.”
        > 
        
        This is the **conversion moment**.
        
        They can:
        
        - continue via email (fine)
        - OR create a NoAgent account (soft-partner)
        
        No pressure.
        
        ---
        
        ## **6️⃣ Secondary level: services (very smart, but subtle)**
        
        Once HH request exists, you can **optionally** add:
        
        > “Would you also like help with surveys, mortgage advice, or conveyancing?”
        > 
        
        This is:
        
        - opt-in
        - separate
        - routed to service partners
        
        Same pattern. Same protection.
        
        ---
        
        ## **7️⃣ Phase 2 upgrade (no redesign needed)**
        
        Later, this evolves naturally into:
        
        - Agent dashboards
        - HH request inbox for agents
        - Real-time preference updates
        - Agent subscriptions to HH profiles
        - Analytics & response time KPIs
        
        But **Phase 1 already works**.
        
        ---
        
        ## **8️⃣ Wireframes affected (clear mapping)**
        
        ### **Home-Hunter**
        
        - **WF-H1 — Dashboard**
            - “Get help from agents” CTA
        - **WF-H5 — Offers & Applications**
            - Request status:
                - Open
                - Agents responding
                - Closed
        
        ### **Admin**
        
        - **WF-A2 — Users**
            - Agent accept / decline metrics
        - **WF-A1 — Dashboard**
            - Requests sent / accepted (later KPI)
        
        ### **Public / Partners**
        
        - **WF-P7 — Partners**
            - Explain request-based model
            - No cold outreach
        
        No new wireframes required.
        
        ---
        
        ## **9️⃣ Why this works (important)**
        
        ### **For Home-Hunters**
        
        - One action
        - No repetition
        - No spam
        - Real choice
        
        ### **For Agents**
        
        - Pre-qualified demand
        - Clear intent
        - Low effort
        - High conversion
        
        ### **For NoAgent**
        
        - Network effects
        - Clean data
        - Trust-first positioning
        - Organic agent onboarding
        
        ---
        
        ## **🔒 Final recommendation (lock it)**
        
        ✔ HH submits **one request**, not many messages
        
        ✔ NoAgent distributes intelligently
        
        ✔ Agents must accept to engage
        
        ✔ HH controls privacy & volume
        
        ✔ Services can be layered later
        
        ✔ Agents are nudged into NoAgent naturally
        
        If you want next, I can:
        
        - write the **exact HH request form fields**
        - draft the **agent email template**
        - or update the **WF-H5 spec** with this logic
        
        This is a *very* strong design — it turns scale into an advantage instead of a problem.
        
    - Adding **“(yet)”** is a *small linguistic tweak*
        
        SpotOn with **big psychological impact**.
        
        The key is to do it **warm, non-threatening, and opportunity-framed**, not passive-aggressive or unfinished.
        
        Below is the **best way to use it**, with exact wording you can safely lock in.
        
        ---
        
        ## **✅ The right framing: capability, not status**
        
        We want agents to think:
        
        > “Ah — this is a lead I can unlock if I join.”
        > 
        
        Not:
        
        > “I’m excluded / they’re against agents.”
        > 
        
        So we avoid words like *partnered*, *blocked*, *unavailable*.
        
        ---
        
        ## **🟢 Recommended final labels (lock these)**
        
        ### **For agents you CAN contact through NoAgent**
        
        **Badge / status:**
        
        > Available via NoAgent
        > 
        
        Clear. Positive. Done.
        
        ---
        
        ### **For agents you CANNOT contact yet (but want to invite)**
        
        **Badge / status (primary recommendation):**
        
        > Not available via NoAgent (yet)
        > 
        
        Why this works:
        
        - “Yet” implies opportunity
        - Neutral, friendly tone
        - Signals *actionability*, not rejection
        - Reads well for Owners **and** HHs
        
        ---
        
        ## **🔁 Alternative softer variants (if you want even warmer)**
        
        You can A/B tone later, but these are safe:
        
        - **Available externally (via NoAgent soon)**
        - **Public agent — available on request**
        - **External agent (can be invited)**
        
        Still good, but **“(yet)” is the clearest nudge**.
        
        ---
        
        ## **🧠 How this reads to different users**
        
        ### **Owner / Home-Hunter**
        
        > “Okay — I can invite them if I want.”
        > 
        
        No confusion. No fear. No salesy pressure.
        
        ### **Agent (when they see themselves)**
        
        > “Interesting. I’m visible, but I could unlock more by joining.”
        > 
        
        Exactly what you want.
        
        ---
        
        ## **🔘 CTA pairing (important)**
        
        Whenever you show:
        
        > Not available via NoAgent (yet)
        > 
        
        The CTA should be:
        
        > Invite this agent to NoAgent
        > 
        
        Not:
        
        - “Contact externally”
        - “Unavailable”
        
        This turns limitation → growth.
        
        ---
        
        ## **🧩 Where this label appears (confirming)**
        
        - **WF-O3 — Find Agents**
        - **WF-H1 — Agent discovery**
        - **WF-P7 — Partners (explained in text)**
        
        ❌ Never shown in Admin (they see real statuses there).
        
        ---
        
        ## **✍️ Optional microcopy (one-liner, tooltip)**
        
        You *can* add a subtle tooltip (optional):
        
        > This agent isn’t reachable through NoAgent yet.
        > 
        
        > You can invite them to receive your request here.
        > 
        
        Keep it short. Don’t overexplain.
        
        ---
        
        ## **🔒 Final recommendation (lock it)**
        
        ✔ Use **“Available via NoAgent”**
        
        ✔ Use **“Not available via NoAgent (yet)”**
        
        ✔ Pair with **Invite CTA**
        
        ✔ Avoid “partnered / unpartnered” entirely
        
        ✔ Keep explanation minimal
        
        This is a **very elegant, human solution** — you’re absolutely right to push for it.
        
        If you want next, I can:
        
        - update the **agent card spec**
        - write the **Invite Agent email copy**
        - or align the same language for **service providers**
        
        This is exactly the level of polish that makes the product feel confident, not defensive.
        
    
    ---
    
    # **How this works in practice (clean + scalable)**
    
    ## **Core principle (lock this in)**
    
    👉 **Agents never browse inboxes.**
    
    👉 **Owners / Home-Hunters initiate contact.**
    
    👉 **NoAgent sends a structured intro on their behalf.**
    
    This keeps:
    
    - trust high
    - spam at zero
    - compliance simple
    
    ---
    
    ## **1️⃣ What the user actually does (Owner or Home-Hunter)**
    
    ### **Step 1 — Search agents (read-only)**
    
    - Search by:
        - postcode (owner)
        - search area (HH)
    - Result = **Agent cards**
        - name
        - coverage area
        - specialties (sales / rentals / new builds)
        - languages (optional, later)
    
    No contact yet.
    
    ---
    
    ### **Step 2 — “Contact agent” (controlled action)**
    
    Button:
    
    > Contact this agent
    > 
    
    Opens a **modal**, not a free text box.
    
    ---
    
    ## **2️⃣ The Contact Modal (THIS is the key)**
    
    ### **The modal has 3 sections**
    
    ### **A) What will be shared (transparent)**
    
    Shown as a preview card:
    
    ### **For Owners**
    
    - Property summary
    - Location (approximate, not full address)
    - Sale / Rent
    - Price range
    - Viewing status
    - Listing quality score (later)
    
    ### **For Home-Hunters**
    
    - Name
    - Buying / renting status
    - Budget range
    - Area(s) of interest
    - Timeline
    - Verification status
    
    👉 **No phone number shared yet**
    
    👉 **No email shared yet**
    
    ---
    
    ### **B) Optional filters (anti-spam control)**
    
    This is your differentiator.
    
    Checkboxes like:
    
    - ☐ Only respond if you work in my postcode
    - ☐ Only contact me if you accept my budget range
    - ☐ Only email (no calls)
    - ☐ No marketing messages
    
    Small copy:
    
    > Your contact details will only be shared if the agent accepts these conditions.
    > 
    
    ---
    
    ### **C) Message intent (structured, not free-form)**
    
    Dropdown:
    
    - “Looking for valuation”
    - “Need help with negotiations”
    - “Considering appointing an agent”
    - “Rental support”
    - “General advice”
    
    Optional short note (max 300 chars).
    
    CTA:
    
    > Send introduction
    > 
    
    ---
    
    ## **3️⃣ What the agent actually receives (important)**
    
    ### **Agents receive a**
    
    ### **single email**
    
    ### **(Phase 1)**
    
    Subject example:
    
    > New verified lead via NoAgent — review & respond
    > 
    
    Email body (structured, clean):
    
    - Summary card (owner or HH)
    - Clear intent
    - Filters / conditions
    - CTA buttons:
        - ✅ Accept & respond
        - ❌ Decline (no action)
    
    👉 No reply-all
    
    👉 No long threads
    
    👉 No inbox chaos
    
    ---
    
    ## **4️⃣ What happens when agent clicks “Accept”**
    
    ### **Phase 1 (simple & safe)**
    
    - Agent clicks **Accept**
    - System:
        - unlocks contact
        - shares email (not phone yet)
        - sends confirmation to Owner / HH:
            
            > “Agent X has accepted your request”
            > 
    
    At this point:
    
    - Communication can move **outside NoAgent**
    - You stay out of the conversation
    - No compliance headache
    
    ---
    
    ## **5️⃣ What if the agent declines or ignores?**
    
    - Decline → nothing shared
    - No response → auto-expire after 7 days
    - Owner / HH can contact another agent
    
    No follow-ups. No reminders. No spam.
    
    ---
    
    ## **6️⃣ Where this lives in your existing wireframes**
    
    ### **✅ Wireframes to update (no new ones)**
    
    ### **WF-O3 — Inquiries & Offers**
    
    - Add:
        - “Find agents” action
        - Contact Agent modal
    
    ### **WF-H1 — Home-Hunter Dashboard**
    
    - Add:
        - “Agents in your area” card
        - Same contact modal
    
    ### **WF-P7 — Partners**
    
    - Explain:
        - how intros work
        - no spam policy
        - why agents benefit
    
    ### **WF-A2 — Users**
    
    - Agent status:
        - invited
        - active
        - accepted leads count
    
    ---
    
    ## **7️⃣ Why this works strategically**
    
    ### **For Owners / HH**
    
    - They stay in control
    - No cold calls
    - No inbox flooding
    - Clear expectations
    
    ### **For Agents**
    
    - Pre-qualified leads
    - Context upfront
    - Less admin
    - Higher conversion
    
    ### **For NoAgent**
    
    - Neutral position
    - Trust brand
    - Clean data
    - Easy Phase-2 expansion
    
    ---
    
    ## **8️⃣ Phase 2 (future, no redesign)**
    
    This same flow can later add:
    
    - In-platform chat
    - Agent dashboards
    - Lead analytics
    - Commission-free handovers
    - Portal publishing by agents
    
    But **nothing changes visually**.
    
    ---
    
    ## **TL;DR (founder version)**
    
    - Use **structured introductions**, not messaging
    - Owner / HH always initiates
    - Agent must accept before contact is shared
    - Filters prevent spam
    - Phase 1 = email only
    - Phase 2 = richer tooling
    
    If you want next, I can:
    
    - write the **exact modal copy**
    - write the **agent email template**
    - or mark this as a **designer-ready delta checklist**
    
    This is a strong, thoughtful feature — and it fits your product philosophy perfectly.
    

# **Designer Job Description & Expectations**

# **NoAgent — Senior UI/UX Designer (Framer + Web SaaS)**

**Project:** Full MVP design for a new property-tech platform (Owner + Home-Hunter + Admin)

**Tagline:** *No agents. No fees. No catch.*

---

# **About NoAgent**

Yalla.House is a new UK-based prop-tech startup reinventing how people list, sell, and find homes — without estate agents.

Think:

**Airbnb-quality UX + Rightmove utility + WhatsApp simplicity.**

We already have:

- Full user journeys
- All wireframes (Owner, Home-Hunter, Admin, Public pages)
- A complete system architecture
- Brand foundations
- A Framer template base (Dashfolio+)

Now we want you — a strong designer — to turn everything into a **polished, consistent, scalable UI ready for development**.

---

# **Your Mission**

Transform our detailed product specification into a **complete, professional, clickable Framer prototype** using the Dashfolio+ base.

You will NOT guess anything.

All flows and components are already defined.

Your job is to **apply design craft**, unify the visual system, and prepare everything for the developer.

---

# **What You Will Deliver (Clear & Complete)**

### **1. Full Framer Project (MVP ready)**

- Setup using our Dashfolio+ template
- Global style system (colors, typography, spacing, shadows, components)
- All screens:
    - Owner Workspace (Dashboard, My Listings, Inquiries, Calendar, Public Pages Preview)
    - Home-Hunter Workspace (Dashboard, Inbox, Saved/Offers, Bookings, Account Settings)
    - Buyer Verification Flow (NEW — see below)
    - Public Pages (Home, Services, About, Property Page, Contact, Legal)
    - Admin Workspace (9 screens, light MVP versions)
    - Unified Account Settings
    - All headers, sidebars, footers, modals, toasts
- Clickable, intuitive navigation

### **2. REQUIRED FEATURE: Buyer Contact Gate UI**

To ensure privacy & create funnel data, buyers must complete a short profile BEFORE they can contact an owner.

You will design:

### **Locked states:**

- “Message Owner (locked)”
- “Book Viewing (locked)”
- “WhatsApp (locked)”
- Greyed-out CTA with lock icon
- Tooltip: *“Verify your profile to continue.”*

### **Unlock Flow:**

- Modal → “Complete Your Profile”
- Fields:
    - Full name
    - Phone number (SMS code flow)
    - Email
    - Buying position (Cash / Mortgage ready / In progress / Browsing)
- SMS verification screen
- Error states
- Success state + redirect
- “Continue to WhatsApp” page
- UI event markers for funnel tracking (dev requirement)

### **After unlocking:**

- All CTAs become active
- Owner receives verified buyer info

---

### **3. Component Library**

Based on Dashfolio+, but extended with:

- Buttons (primary, ghost, locked)
- Form inputs
- Step banners
- Cards (property, offer, inquiry, survey)
- Modals (confirmation, profile, upload)
- Calendar elements
- KPI widgets
- Tables (Owner, Home-Hunter, Admin)
- Icons (we use Lucide)
- Notifications & error states

---

### **4. Responsive Design**

- Full desktop design required
- Optimised for mobile (public pages + booking flow especially)

---

### **5. Documentation Provided Inside Framer**

You will create a short “Design Notes” page describing:

- Component usage rules
- Font sizes
- Spacing
- Button hierarchies
- Colour semantics (success, info, warning, error)
- Any deviations/extensions from Dashfolio+

---

### **6. Up to 3 Revision Cycles**

We expect a clean iteration process.

No test tasks — we pay for professional work.

---

# **Your Skills**

We need someone who reliably delivers in a startup environment:

### **Required**

- Strong UI/UX for SaaS or marketplaces
- Framer mastery (essential)
- Can build full multi-screen flows
- Ability to convert written flows + wireframes into clean UI
- Experience designing dashboards and complex forms
- Fluent English
- Independent, organised, communicates clearly

### **Bonus (moves you to the front of the queue)**

- You can ALSO implement in Framer (basic dev layer)
- OR
- You want to take the **Developer Job** next.
    
    (We hire designers first, then developers — but full-stack designers get priority.)
    

---

# **Scope & Timeline**

- Start: Immediately
- Duration: ~3–4 weeks
- Output: Full clickable MVP in Framer

---

# **Budget**

Flexible based on experience.

We prefer quality over speed, but want clean, structured work.

- Designer Workspace in Notion
- All wireframes

- Brand assets
- All UX notes
- Clarification log
- Founder availability for decisions

We keep everything extremely organised — you will not need to chase information.

    3. **Manage Listing** (tabs)
    4. **Preview** always routes to **WF-O5**
    5. **Publish Plan (+1)** triggered from WF-O5 (not a sidebar item)
    
    > Rule:
    > 
    
    ---
    
    # **A) Inventory Table (Default View)**
    
    ## **Purpose**
    
    Show all listings at a glance and give fast actions: **Manage** + **Preview**.
    
    ## **Table Columns (Phase 1)**
    
    - Thumbnail
    - Title (short address label)
    - **Intent**: Sale / Rent
    - **Status**: Draft / Live / Under Offer / Let Agreed / Sold / Let
    - Price (with label)
    - Views (7d)
    - Last activity
    - Actions: **Manage** / **Preview (WF-O5)**
    
    ## **Behaviours (Phase 1)**
    
    - Row click → opens **Manage Listing**
    - **Add Listing** button → opens Wizard Step 1
    - Preview always available from row action
    
    ## **Filters (Phase 1 — light)**
    
    - Status: All / Draft / Live / Under Offer / Sold (auto adapts for rent)
    - Intent: Sale / Rent
    
    ## **Empty State (no listings)**
    
    **Headline:** “Create your first listing.”
    
    **Body:** “It takes around 10 minutes. You can preview before publishing.”
    
    CTA: **Add Listing**
    
    ---
    
    # **B) Create Listing Wizard (Steps 1–5) — v1.4**
    
    ## **Wizard shell rules**
    
    - Step progress (1–5)
    - **Save & exit** always visible
    - Back / Continue pinned bottom bar
    - Required vs Optional clearly marked
    - Autosave each step
    
    ---
    
    ## **Step 1 — Basics (creates Draft listing)**
    
    ### **Fields**
    
    - **Property address** (required)
    - **Property type** (required)
    - **Intent** (required): **For Sale / To Rent** *(selected once only)*
    
    ### **System note (small, muted) — show under primary CTA**
    
    > Once you save this step, your listing is created in Draft so you can preview and manage viewings before publishing.
    > 
    
    ### **Locked behaviour**
    
    - Saving Step 1 creates listing in **Draft** and assigns permanent internal reference used across previews, sharing, bookings, QR codes, and portal feeds.
    
    ---
    
    ## **Step 2 — Price**
    
    ### **Fields**
    
    - Asking price (required)
    - Price label (required) — **locked options**
        - **Offers over**
        - **Negotiable (around that price)**
        - **Shared Ownership**
    - Currency (read-only, required) — based on country config
    
    ### **Shared Ownership (only if selected)**
    
    - Share available % (optional)
    - Full market value (optional)
    - Rent estimate (optional)
    
    ---
    
    ## **Step 3 — Details**
    
    ### **Core fields**
    
    - Bedrooms (required)
    - Bathrooms (required)
    - Size + unit (required)
    - Short description (required) *(microcopy adapts to Sale vs Rent)*
    - **Key Features** (optional chips/tags)
    
    ### **UK-only fields**
    
    - Council Tax Band (optional) — UK only
    - Tenure (optional) — UK + Sale only
    
    ---
    
    ## **Step 4 — Media & Documents**
    
    ### **Fields**
    
    - Photos (required) — minimum 5
    - Floorplan (optional)
    - EPC (optional, country-dependent)
    - Other documents (optional)
    
    > Publish is blocked
    > 
    
    ---
    
    ## **Step 5 — Finish & Preview**
    
    ### **Components**
    
    - Completion checklist (read-only ✅ / ⚠ with “Edit” deep links)
    - Primary CTA: **Preview listing (WF-O5)**
    - Secondary CTA: **Save Draft & return to table**
    
    > Preview is the confidence moment.
    > 
    
    ---
    
    # **+1 Publish Plan (After Preview only)  Phase 1**
    
    > Not a sidebar page.
    > 
    > 
    > **WF-O5**
    > 
    
    ### **What appears**
    
    - Plan cards (3)
    - Country-specific portal options (where available)
    - Partner services add-ons (optional)
    - Checkout (Stripe) only if paid options chosen
    
    ### **Calendar confirmation mode (LOCKED)**
    
    During Publish Plan, show one simple choice (radio):
    
    - **Manual confirmation (recommended)**
    - **Auto-confirm bookings**
    
    This is saved per listing and shown in:
    
    - WF-O4 Calendar
    - WF-O5 booking CTA (Request vs Book instantly)
    - WF-H3 booking status (Pending vs Confirmed)
    
    ---
    
    # **C) Manage Listing (Per Listing) — Tabs (Phase 1)**
    
    ## **Listing header**
    
    Shows:
    
    - Address/title
    - Status chip
    - Actions:
        - **Preview (WF-O5)**
        - Change status
        - (Optional) Share link
    
    ## **Tabs**
    
    1. **Details**
    2. **Photos & Media**
    3. **Documents**
    4. **Publication & Status**
    
    ### **Status rules**
    
    - Sold / Let → disables booking & messaging CTAs publicly
    - Under Offer / Let Agreed → shows banner on public page
    
    ---
    
    # **🔒 Phase-1 Locked Behaviours (summary)**
    
    - Step 1 save → listing exists as **Draft**
    - Preview (WF-O5) always accessible from table, manage view, and Step 5
    - Publish Plan (+1) happens **only after preview**
    - Booking confirmation defaults to **Manual**, auto-confirm optional per listing
    - Public CTAs and banners adapt to status
    
    ---
    
    # **✍️ Dummy content for design**
    
    Listings table examples:
    
    - “12 Park Road, IG2” — Live — **Offers over £525,000** — 182 views
    - “Flat 4, 19 High St” — Draft — **€1,650 pcm (Negotiable)** — 0 views
    - “7 Linden Ave” — Under Offer — **£612,500** — 96 views
    
    ---
    
- **🧩 WF-O5 — Public Property Page (old)**
    
    **Modes:** Public · Home-Hunter · Owner Preview
    
    **Core principle:** **Booking-first. No dead ends. Owner stays in control.**
    
    ---
    
    ## **🎯 Purpose (Final)**
    
    WF-O5 is the **primary conversion surface** of NoAgent.
    
    It must:
    
    1. Show the property clearly
    2. Surface **real availability immediately**
    3. Convert interest into **scheduled viewings**
    4. Provide a **request fallback** when no slots exist
    5. Reflect **confirmation rules set by the Owner**
    6. Let Owners preview *exactly* what Home-Hunters see
    
    > This is **not a brochure page.**
    > 
    
    > It is a **calendar-led booking page with a safety net.**
    > 
    
    ---
    
    ## **📍 Routes & Entry Points**
    
    - Public: /property/:slug
    - Owner Preview: /owner/property/:id/preview or ?preview=true
    
    Entry from:
    
    - Portals / feed aggregators
    - QR codes / shares
    - Owner workspace (WF-O1 / WF-O2)
    - Direct links
    
    ---
    
    ## **🧱 Page Structure (Top → Bottom)**
    
    ```
    [ Hero Media ]
    [ Key Facts Strip ]
    [ AVAILABILITY PREVIEW (Above the fold) ]
    [ Primary CTA Row ]
    [ Description ]
    [ Features ]
    [ Documents ]
    [ Map ]
    [ FULL CALENDAR / REQUEST VIEWING ]
    [ Trust & Context ]
    ```
    
    ---
    
    ## **1️⃣ Hero Media (unchanged)**
    
    - Photo carousel (hero image first)
    - Image counter
    - Optional video / 360 badge (Phase 2)
    
    **Owner Preview only**
    
    - Badge: *Owner Preview*
    - Button: **Edit listing** → WF-O2
    
    ---
    
    ## **2️⃣ Key Facts Strip (unchanged)**
    
    Always visible:
    
    - Price (sale / rent)
    - Status badge: **For Sale / To Rent**
    - Beds · Baths · Size
    - Property type
    
    ---
    
    ## **⭐ 3️⃣ Availability Preview — ABOVE THE FOLD (Primary Conversion)**
    
    ### **Purpose**
    
    Answer instantly:
    
    > “Can I view this place?”
    > 
    
    ---
    
    ### **Availability Preview Card**
    
    ---
    
    ### **✅ Case A — Slots Available**
    
    Shows:
    
    - Title: **Next available viewings**
    - Up to **3 upcoming slots**, e.g.
        - Sat 11:00 — Group viewing
        - Tue 17:30 — Private viewing
    
    Each slot shows a **status hint**:
    
    - *Instant booking* → auto-confirm listing
    - *Request to book* → manual confirmation listing
    
    Primary CTA:
    
    - 🔶 **Arrange a Visit**
    
    **Interaction**
    
    - Click slot or CTA:
        - Not verified → verification gate
        - Verified → booking flow (WF-H1)
    
    ---
    
    ### **Owner Preview (read-only)**
    
    Helper text (muted):
    
    > This is how Home-Hunters see your availability and booking options.
    > 
    
    ---
    
    ### **🚫 Case B — No Slots Available (Fallback)**
    
    Shows:
    
    ```
    No viewings available right now.
    
    [ Request a Viewing ]
    ```
    
    Helper text:
    
    > The owner will be notified and can add availability.
    > 
    
    Rules:
    
    - Verification required
    - Creates a **Viewing Request**, not a booking
    
    ---
    
    ## **4️⃣ Primary CTA Row (Locked Hierarchy)**
    
    1. 🔶 **Arrange a Visit** (Primary)
    2. **Message Owner** (Secondary)
    3. **Save Property** (Tertiary)
    
    ### **Locked state (not verified)**
    
    - Booking + Messaging show lock icon
    - Tooltip:
        
        > Verify your profile to book or message.
        > 
    
    ---
    
    ## **5️⃣ Description (unchanged)**
    
    - Expand / collapse
    - Editable by Owner (WF-O2)
    
    ---
    
    ## **6️⃣ Features & Highlights (unchanged)**
    
    Displayed as chips:
    
    - Balcony · Garden · Parking · Furnished · Freehold / Leasehold
    
    ---
    
    ## **7️⃣ Documents (unchanged)**
    
    Public (if enabled):
    
    - Floorplan
    - EPC
    - Brochure
    
    **Owner Preview**
    
    - Toggle public/private
    - Edit → WF-O2
    
    ---
    
    ## **8️⃣ Map & Location (unchanged)**
    
    - Approximate pin
    - Area name
    - StreetView preview
    - Exact address hidden (Phase 1)
    
    ---
    
    ## **⭐ 9️⃣ Full Calendar / Request Section (Below the Fold)**
    
    ### **If slots exist**
    
    - Embedded live calendar (from WF-O4)
    - Week / Day toggle
    - Group / Private labels
    - Slot click → booking flow
    
    ### **If no slots**
    
    ```
    No availability has been added yet.
    
    [ Request a Viewing ]
    ```
    
    ---
    
    ## **📨 Request a Viewing — Modal (Locked)**
    
    **Title:** Request a viewing
    
    **Fields**
    
    - Preferred timeframe:
        - Weekday mornings
        - Weekday evenings
        - Weekends
        - Flexible
    - Optional message
    
    **CTA**
    
    - 🔶 **Send request**
    
    ---
    
    ## **🔁 Owner Side Effects (System Behaviour)**
    
    When a request is sent:
    
    - Creates a **Viewing Request event**
    - Appears in:
        - WF-O3 — Inquiries
        - WF-O4 — Calendar (prompt state)
    - Owner can:
        - Add availability (deep link)
        - Message Home-Hunter
        - Ignore / dismiss
    
    Limits:
    
    - One request per Home-Hunter per listing
    - Requests expire after X days (e.g. 7)
    
    ---
    
    ## **🔁 Behaviour by Role (Final)**
    
    | **Feature** | **Public** | **Home-Hunter (Verified)** | **Owner** |
    | --- | --- | --- | --- |
    | See availability | ✅ | ✅ | ✅ |
    | Book viewing | 🔒 | ✅ | ❌ |
    | Request viewing | 🔒 | ✅ | ❌ |
    | Message owner | 🔒 | ✅ | ❌ |
    | Save property | ✅ | ✅ | ❌ |
    | Edit listing | ❌ | ❌ | ✅ |
    
    ---
    
    ## **🔒 Phase-1 Locks (WF-O5)**
    
    - Availability always visible
    - Booking CTA adapts to confirmation mode
    - Manual confirmation = “Request to book”
    - Auto-confirm = “Instant booking”
    - Request flow never bypasses owner control
    - Owner preview = exact public page
    
    ---
    
    ## **STATEMENT — WF-O5**
    
    > WF-O5 is a booking-first public page with a controlled fallback.
    > 
    
    > Home-Hunters always see availability or a request option.
    > 
    
    > Booking behaviour reflects the Owner’s confirmation settings.
    > 
    
    > Owners preview the exact live page used by links, QR codes, and portals — with no dead ends and no pressure.
    > 
    
    ---
